data-reactid="145"><span data-reactid="146">4 side servings</span></span><span data-reactid="147"></span></div><h2 class="dek--basically" data-reactid="148">This recipe is one of our favorites from <em><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Maangchis-Big-Book-Korean-Cooking/dp/1328988120" data-amzn-asin="1328988120">Maangchi's Big Book of Korean Cooking</a></em>, our December 2019 pick for <em>BA</em>âs Cookbook Club. We like to think of this sweet and salty dish as a sort of vegetarian bulgogi. Marinating and pan-frying eggplant keeps it firm, flavorful, and chewyâalmost meaty. The marinade glazes it as it cooks, so it glistens. Prepared this way, the eggplant looks very special, even though the recipe is easy. Itâs a versatile dish that makes a great side for rice and many other preparations. The eggplant tastes wonderful right off the stove, but itâs even better after a few hours, when all the flavors have had time to mingle and deepen. Seek out Korean eggplants, if possible, which are sold in Korean markets. They are thinner than ordinary eggplants and the skin is more tender. But regular eggplants work, too.</h2><div class="print-row-container align-to-container" data-reactid="149"><a href="/search?content=recipe&amp;issueDate=2019-11-01" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-reactid="150"><div class="MonthYear" data-reactid="151">November 2019</div></a><button class="basically_print_button" data-reactid="152">Print</button></div></div></div><div Toss well by hand until all eggplant is salted. Let sit, tossing every 5 minutes, for 20 minutes.</p></div></li><li class="step" data-reactid="202"><div data-reactid="203"><p data-reactid="204">Drain eggplant; discard liquid. Take up handfuls of eggplant and squeeze tightly to remove excess liquid, then return to large bowl. Add marinade to bowl with eggplant and mix together well. Cover and chill 30 minutes.</p></div></li><li class="step" data-reactid="205"><div data-reactid="206"><p data-reactid="207">Heat oil in a large heavy skillet over medium-high and swirl to coat pan evenly. Add marinated eggplant and spread evenly in skillet. Leave to sear for a few minutes, until bottom is lightly colored. Turn with a spatula or tongs and cook until other side is lightly browned, 2â3 minutes. Reduce heat to medium and continue to cook, pressing eggplant into pan and turning from time to time, until eggplant is cooked through and glazed and any excess marinade has evaporated, 5â6 minutes.</p></div></li><li class="step" data-reactid="208"><div data-reactid="209"><p data-reactid="210">Transfer eggplant to a plate. Sprinkle with sesame seeds. Serve hot or cold.</p></div></li><li class="step" data-reactid="211"><div data-reactid="212"><p data-reactid="213"><strong data-reactid="214">Do Ahead:</strong><!-- react-text: 215 --> Eggplant can be made 3 days ahead. Store in an airtight container and chill.<!-- /react-text --></p></div></li></ul></div></div><div class="row util-print-hide" data-component="Row" data-reactid="216"><div class="contributors" data-reactid="217"><div class="contributor contributor-recipe-author" data-reactid="218"><span class="contributor-type" data-reactid="219">Recipe by </span><span class="contributor-name" data-reactid="220">Excerpted from Maangchiâs Big Book of Korean Cooking: From Everyday Meals to Celebration Cuisine Â©ï¸ 2019 by Maangchi. alt="" data-reactid="250"></div><div class="review-body" data-reactid="251">I was really excited to make this but it turned out very bland. The salt did not draw out as much liquid as I anticipated, even after leaving it for longer than the recipe recommends--so I really had to squeeze the heck out of small handfuls to get the incredible amount of water out of the eggplants. I think it was bland because the marinade did not have enough liquid in it. I used sugar instead of rice syrup--so the marinade only had 1 tbsp of liquid in it, rather than 1/4 c + 1 tbsp. Next time I'll either add water or more soy sauce to the marinade. Bummer but we'll get it next time. </div><div class="review-byline" data-reactid="252"><span class="review-author" data-reactid="253">JohnSpringer</span><span class="review-location" data-reactid="254">Kansas City, MO</span><span class="review-datestamp" data-reactid="255">12/08/19</span></div></div></div></div></div><div class="col col-xs-4 col-sm-12 col-md-4 col--MainWithSidebar col--secondary" data-component="Col" data-reactid="256"><div data-reactid="257"><div class="component-stickybox component-stickybox-ba" data-component="Stickybox" style="height: auto;" data-reactid="258"><div class="inner" style="width: auto;" data-reactid="259"><div class="sticky-video-target stuck" data-reactid="260"></div><div class="cns--box_top" data-reactid="261"><div id="cns-ads-slot-type-box-top-0" class="cns-ads-stage cns-ads-slot-type-box-top cns-ads-slot-type-box-top-0 cns-ads-slot-state-filled cns-ads-slot-size-300x600" data-name="box_top_0" data-slot-type="box_top" style="font-size: 0px;
